is one of the most played board games in the world, play with your friends, try to defeat your opponents with strategy, reasoning and a little bit of luck.\r\nGeneral rules of dominoes:\r\n- Blocking game\r\nThe most basic dominos variant is for two players and requires a double six set. The 28 domino tiles are shuffled face down and form the stock or boneyard. Each player draws seven tiles; the remainder are not used. Once the players begin drawing tiles, they are typically placed on-edge before the players, so that each player can see his own domino tiles, but none can see the value of other players' tiles. Every player can thus see how many tiles remain in the other players' hands at all times during gameplay. One player begins by downing (playing the first tile) one of their tiles. In different games first tiles are also different. In Muggins player should start with the highest double (6-6), in Bergen the first move should be 0-0, in Mexican train each round starts with the next lower double. This tile starts the line of play, a series of tiles in which adjacent tiles touch with matching, i.e. equal, values. The players alternately extend the line of play with one tile at one of its two ends. The game ends when one player wins by playing their last tile, or when the game is blocked because neither player can play. If that occurs, whoever caused the block gets all of the remaining player points not counting their own.\r\n- Scoring game\r\nPlayers accrue points during game play for certain configurations, moves, or emptying one's hand. Most scoring games use variations of the draw game. In Muggins (All fives) player must make the open ends of the layout add up to 5s or a multiple of five (5s, 10, 15, 20, etc.) In bergen player scores when numbers on the open ends are equal. If a player does not call \"domino\" before the tile is laid on the table, and another player says 'domino' after the tile is laid, the first player must pick up an extra domino. In Mexican train the double zero domino is scored as 50 points.\r\n- Draw game\r\nIn a draw game (blocking or scoring), players are additionally allowed to draw as many tiles as desired from the stock before playing a tile. The score of a game is the number of pips in the losing player's hand plus the number of pips in the stock. Most rules prescribe that two tiles need to remain in the stock. The Draw game is often referred to as simply \"dominos\".\r\n\r\nIf you like board games like Checkers, Mahjong, Backgammon and Chess, you will love Dominoes: Best Classic Dominoes Board Game.","ProductFamilyName":"Games","Schema":"Card;1"},{"$type":"Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts.V8.One.CardModel, Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts","ProductId":"9MTDJMPVNKN2","TileLayout":"Poster","Title":"Basketball Shoot NBA Stars","Images":[{"$type":"Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts.V2.ImageItem, Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts","ImageType":"tile","Url":"http://store-images.s-microsoft.com/image/apps.3647.13809967470494297.62c20468-ccea-4166-9351-1ba5cbda6181.6ea37e8b-4fe8-43f3-adbf-8209479a6f85","Height":300,"Width":300,"BackgroundColor":"#ffffff","ForegroundColor":"","Caption":"","ImagePositionInfo":""},{"$type":"Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts.V2.ImageItem, Microsoft.Marketplace.Storefront.Contracts","ImageType":"tile","Url":"http://store-images.s-microsoft.com/image/apps.47031.13809967470494297.62c20468-ccea-4166-9351-1ba5cbda6181.6a70d50a-0a62-4f4f-865b-fb78bb74c1fd","Height":300,"Width":620,"BackgroundColor":"#ffffff","ForegroundColor":"","Caption":"","ImagePositionInfo":""}],"DisplayPrice":"Kostenlos","Price":0.0,"AverageRating":0.0,"RatingsCount":"0","PackageFamilyNames":["23790BitMangoGames.BasketballShootNBAStars_zcfjb2tswwhgj"],"ContentIds":["f7c07237-0bab-a9e6-968a-63f480e5da47","ac5b7951-e4b5-a21c-8d56-4e407a6d7445"],"GamingOptionsXboxLive":false,"AvailableDevicesDisplayText":"","AvailableDevicesNarratorText":"PC","TypeTag":"app","RecommendationReason":"","LongDescription":"Like scoring the baskets in basketball? Skizziere deine Ideen mit natürlichen Werkzeugen und vektorbasierten Strichen auf einer unendlichen Leinwand und passe sie anschließend mit intuitiven Gesten an. Wenn du bereit für Feedback bist, kannst du es jederzeit und überall mit Kollegen und Freunden teilen.\n\n- Mit flüssigen und organischen Pinseln skizzieren, gestalten und notieren. Unsere realistischen Werkzeuge reagieren auf Druck, Neigung sowie Geschwindigkeit und bleiben beim Zoomen kristallklar. \n- Für grenzenlose Fantasie und Kreativität über die unendliche Leinwand zoomen und schwenken.\n- Benutzeroberfläche für einen komfortablen, fokussierten Arbeitsablauf individuell anpassen.\n- Acht anpassbare Werkzeugschlitze, Werkzeugvoreinstellungen für Größe, Deckkraft und Glättung und das wunderschöne COPIC-Farbrad, mit dem man Farben auswählen können, die immer wieder fantastisch aussehen.\n- Tippen und Halten, um einen beliebigen Teil (oder alles) deiner Skizze auszuwählen und anzupassen, zu optimieren, zu kopieren und mit natürlichen Gesten zu verschieben.\n- Bilder als Referenzmaterialien importieren oder sie als Teil deiner Designs einsetzen.\n- Unbegrenztes Rückgängigmachen mit einem Zwei-Finger-Tipp auf dem Bildschirm.\n- Unendliche, einstellbare Ebenen mit automatischer werkzeugbasierter Sortierung hilft dir, deine Arbeit zu organisieren.\n- Hintergrundpapiertyp oder eine benutzerdefinierte Hintergrundfarbe auswählen.\n- Fingeraktion so einstellen, dass sie etwas getrennt von deinem Stylus macht, wie z. B. Schwenken oder Auswählen. \n- Export in Standard- und hochauflösende Formate für schönen Druck und schnelles Feedback zwischen Kollegen und Freunden.\n\nTop-Designern bei Disney, Playstation, Philips, HP, Apple, Unity, Illumination Entertainment und weiteren verwenden Concepts.\n\n- „Ich nutze Concepts mehr als jedes andere Tool.
